## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-k8s-arch-001: Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture

## Task

Explain the Kubernetes scheduler architecture and how a Pod gets assigned to a Node. Trace the complete scheduling pipeline from when a Pod enters the scheduling queue to when it is bound to a Node, including the plugin framework, extension points, and the two-phase (scheduling cycle + binding cycle) design.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~2.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: pkg/scheduler/ — the kube-scheduler component

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the scheduler subsystem (scheduler core, framework, queue, cache, plugins)
2. Trace the dependency chain from the main scheduling loop through the scheduling cycle and binding cycle
3. Document the plugin framework architecture (extension points: PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit, Bind)
4. Explain how the SchedulingQueue, Cache, and CycleState interact during a scheduling cycle

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

     1→# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis
     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→The Kubernetes scheduler is responsible for assigning unscheduled Pods to Nodes. It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## Files Examined
    10→
    11→### Core Scheduler Files
    12→- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points
    13→- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)
    14→
    15→### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure
    16→- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types
    17→- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage
    18→- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution
    19→
    20→### Scheduling Queue & Cache
    21→- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods
    22→- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — `ca
... (truncated)

## Summary of Analysis

### **Files Examined (13 key files)**
I identified and analyzed all architecturally relevant files including:
- Core scheduler orchestration: `scheduler.go`, `schedule_one.go`
- Framework: `interface.go`, `cycle_state.go`, `runtime/framework.go`
- Queue/Cache: `scheduling_queue.go`, `cache.go`, `node_tree.go`, `snapshot.go`
- Integration: `eventhandlers.go`, `extender.go`

### **Dependency Chain Traced**
Complete flow from initialization through binding:
1. **Entry Point**: `scheduler.New()` → `sched.Run()`
2. **Main Loop**: `ScheduleOne()` continuously pops pods from queue
3. **Scheduling Cycle**: Filtering (PreFilter→Filter) → Scoring (PreScore→Score) → Selection → Assume → Reserve → Permit
4. **Binding Cycle**: WaitOnPermit → PreBind → Bind → PostBind

### **Architecture Analysis Covers**
- **6 Design Patterns**: Plugin framework, two-phase design, state isolation, assume-release, queue-based requeuing, snapshot isolation
- **Component Responsibilities**: Scheduler, Framework, Queue, Cache, Plugins
- **Data Flow**: Detailed diagrams of scheduling and binding cycle flows
- **Interface Contracts**: All plugin types, Status codes, Handle interface
- **Queue Integration**: State management and event-driven requeuing
- **Error Handling**: Recovery mechanisms for both cycle phases

### **Key Insights**
The scheduler achieves high throughput and correctness through:
- **12 Extension Points** enabling flexible scheduling policies
- **Two-Phase Design** separating selection (sync) from commitment (async)
- **CycleState** for plugin-to-plugin communication without coupling

Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all {
  "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler is responsible for assigning unscheduled Pods to Nodes. It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** \u2014 Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** \u2014 Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)\n\n### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** \u2014 Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** \u2014 `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** \u2014 `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** \u2014 `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** \u2014 `cacheImpl` maintaining node information, tracking assumed pods, and managing cache assumptions\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** \u2014 Tree structure for efficient node lookup\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** \u2014 Immutable snapshot of cache taken at scheduling cycle start\n\n### Event Handling & Extenders\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** \u2014 Event handlers for pod/node/storage class updates triggering queue requeuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** \u2014 HTTP-based external scheduler extender interface\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. **Entry Point: Scheduler Initialization & Run**\n   - **`scheduler.New(ctx, client, informerFactory, ...)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:253)\n     - Creates in-tree plugin registry\n     - Builds scheduler profiles and framework instances\n     - Initializes scheduling queue (PriorityQueue)\n     - Initializes scheduler cache\n     - Registers event handlers for pods/nodes\n     - Returns `*Scheduler` instance\n\n   - **`sched.Run(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435)\n     - Starts scheduling queue goroutines\n     - Launches main scheduling loop via `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)`\n\n### 2. **Main Scheduling Loop**\n   - **`sched.ScheduleOne(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66)\n     - Calls `sched.NextPod(logger)` \u2192 pops from `SchedulingQueue`\n     - Retrieves framework for pod's scheduler name\n     - Calls **`sched.schedulingCycle(ctx, state, fwk, podInfo, start, podsToActivate)`** (line 111)\n     - On success, launches binding cycle in goroutine\n\n### 3. **Scheduling Cycle (Pod Selection)**\n   - **`schedulingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:139)\n     1. Calls **`sched.SchedulePod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`** \u2192 **`sched.schedulePod()`** (line 390)\n        - Updates cache snapshot via `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n        - **Phase A: Filtering**\n          - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`\n          - Runs **PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` (line 453)\n          - Calls **`findNodesThatPassFilters()`** (line 573)\n            - Runs **Filter plugins** in parallel via `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` (line 640)\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)` per node\n          - Processes extender filters via `findNodesThatPassExtenders()`\n        - **Phase B: Scoring**\n          - Calls **`prioritizeNodes()`** (line 425)\n          - Runs **PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n          - Runs **Score plugins** on each feasible node via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n          - Scores with extenders (if present)\n        - **Phase C: Selection**\n          - Calls `selectHost()` to pick best-scored node\n\n     2. On success, **assumes pod** via `sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, nodeName)` (line 198)\n        - Adds pod to cache with assumed state\n\n     3. Runs **Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` (line 209)\n        - If fails, calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n\n     4. Runs **Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` (line 231)\n        - Creates waiting pods if any plugin returns \"Wait\"\n\n### 4. **Binding Cycle (Pod Commitment)**\n   - **`bindingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:265)\n     1. Waits on **Permit plugins** via `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` (line 278)\n\n     2. Runs **PreBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` (line 294)\n        - Performs pre-binding validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n\n     3. Runs **Bind plugins** via `sched.bind()` (line 299)\n        - Default: calls API server to create Pod binding\n        - Can be overridden by custom bind plugins\n\n     4. Runs **PostBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` (line 312)\n        - Informational, performs cleanup/logging\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Plugin Framework Architecture**\nThe scheduler uses an **extension point** pattern where plugins implement specific interfaces and hook into well-defined points in the scheduling pipeline:\n\n```\nExtension Points (in execution order):\n\u251c\u2500 PreEnqueue (before pod enters activeQ)\n\u251c\u2500 QueueSort (sorts pods in queue)\n\u251c\u2500 PreFilter (pod-level filtering setup, can filter out nodes)\n\u251c\u2500 Filter (per-node filtering, parallel execution)\n\u251c\u2500 PostFilter (preemption/recovery if no nodes fit)\n\u251c\u2500 PreScore (informational, after filtering)\n\u251c\u2500 Score (per-node scoring, parallel execution)\n\u251c\u2500 Reserve (mark node as having resources reserved)\n\u251c\u2500 Permit (final gate before binding, can wait)\n\u251c\u2500 PreBind (validation before binding)\n\u251c\u2500 Bind (performs actual binding)\n\u2514\u2500 PostBind (post-binding cleanup)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n- **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Evaluates pods/nodes, makes scheduling decision\n- **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Commits binding to API server without blocking other scheduling\n\nThis enables the scheduler to continue scheduling other pods while binding happens asynchronously.\n\n#### 3. **State Isolation via CycleState**\nEach scheduling cycle creates a fresh `CycleState` that plugins use to store temporary data:\n- Thread-safe storage using `sync.Map`\n- Plugins write computed state in PreFilter/PreScore\n- Other plugins read this state in Filter/Score\n- Allows plugins to share information without direct coupling\n\n#### 4. **Assume-Release Pattern**\nBefore binding completes, the pod is \"assumed\" in the cache:\n- Updates cache immediately after successful Reserve phase\n- Allows next scheduling cycle to see \"reserved\" resources\n- If binding fails later, cache is updated via `ForgetPod()`\n- Prevents scheduling multiple pods to same space\n\n#### 5. **Queue-based Requeuing**\nPods move through queue states based on scheduling outcome:\n```\nPod States in Queue:\n\u251c\u2500 activeQ: Ready to be scheduled\n\u251c\u2500 backoffQ: Unschedulable but will retry after backoff\n\u2514\u2500 unschedulablePods: Unschedulable, stays until cluster event triggers requeue\n```\n\n#### 6. **Snapshot Isolation**\nCache snapshot taken at cycle start ensures consistent view throughout filtering/scoring:\n- Prevents race conditions between cycle phases\n- Snapshot remains unchanged during Permit phase\n- Binding cycle may see different cluster state (acceptable)\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n#### **Scheduler (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go)**\n- Orchestrates overall scheduling workflow\n- Maintains cache and queue\n- Manages framework profiles (supports multiple scheduler instances)\n- Registers event handlers to respond to cluster changes\n\n#### **Framework (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go)**\n- Loads and initializes plugins\n- Routes scheduling requests through plugin extension points\n- Manages plugin execution (sequential or parallel)\n- Provides Handle interface for plugins to access cluster state\n\n#### **SchedulingQueue (pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go)**\n- Maintains pod queues with priority\n- Moves pods between queues based on scheduling outcomes\n- Integrates with plugins for event-driven requeuing\n- Supports backoff for failed pods\n\n#### **Cache (pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go)**\n- Maintains node information (CPU, memory, pods)\n- Tracks assumed pods with configurable TTL\n- Provides snapshots for consistent scheduling cycles\n- Expires long-lived assumptions automatically\n\n#### **Plugins (via plugin interfaces in framework/interface.go)**\n- **PreFilter/Filter**: Determine node feasibility\n- **Score**: Rank feasible nodes\n- **Reserve/Permit**: Gate decisions before binding\n- **Bind/PreBind/PostBind**: Manage binding lifecycle\n- **PostFilter**: Implement preemption or recovery logic\n\n### Data Flow\n\n#### **Scheduling Cycle Data Flow**\n```\nPod from Queue\n    \u2193\n[CycleState created]\n    \u2193\n[Cache Snapshot taken]\n    \u2193\nRunPreFilterPlugins() \u2190 Plugins can exclude entire node sets\n    \u2193\nRunFilterPlugins() on each node (parallel) \u2190 Per-node feasibility\n    \u2193\n[Feasible nodes list]\n    \u2193\nRunPreScorePlugins() \u2190 Informational, prepare scoring state\n    \u2193\nRunScorePlugins() on feasible nodes (parallel) \u2190 Rank nodes\n    \u2193\nselectHost() \u2190 Pick highest-scored node\n    \u2193\nCache.AssumedPodAdded() \u2190 Reserve resources in cache\n    \u2193\nRunReservePlugins() \u2190 Plugins update internal state\n    \u2193\nRunPermitPlugins() \u2190 Final gate (can wait)\n    \u2193\nReturn: Success \u2192 Launch Binding Cycle\n```\n\n#### **Binding Cycle Data Flow**\n```\n[From Scheduling Cycle: Assumed Pod Info]\n    \u2193\nWaitOnPermit() \u2190 Block if Permit returned \"Wait\"\n    \u2193\nRunPreBindPlugins() \u2190 Validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n    \u2193\nRunBindPlugins() \u2190 Commit to API server\n    \u2193\nRunPostBindPlugins() \u2190 Cleanup/logging\n    \u2193\nQueue.Done() \u2190 Mark pod processing complete\n    \u2193\nSuccess: Pod bound to node\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go:329)**\nAll plugins must implement:\n```go\ntype Plugin interface {\n    Name() string\n}\n```\n\n#### **Extension Point Interfaces**\n- **PreFilterPlugin** \u2192 `PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)`\n- **FilterPlugin** \u2192 `Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) *Status`\n- **ScorePlugin** \u2192 `Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, *Status)`\n- **ReservePlugin** \u2192 `Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n- **PermitPlugin** \u2192 `Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (*Status, time.Duration)`\n- **BindPlugin** \u2192 `Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n\n#### **Status Codes**\n- `Success` (nil): Operation succeeded\n- `Unschedulable`: Pod doesn't fit (might succeed after preemption)\n- `UnschedulableAndUnresolvable`: Pod doesn't fit (preemption won't help)\n- `Wait`: Permit plugin wants to wait before binding\n- `Error`: Unexpected failure\n- `Pending`: Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external action\n\n#### **Framework Handle Interface (framework/interface.go:663)**\nPlugins receive `Handle` providing:\n- `SnapshotSharedLister()` \u2192 Access to node/pod cache snapshots\n- `ClientSet()` \u2192 Kubernetes client\n- `EventRecorder()` \u2192 Record events\n- Waiting pod management\n- Pod nominator for preemption hints\n\n### Queue Integration\n\n#### **Scheduling Queue States**\n- **activeQ**: Heap of pods ready to schedule, sorted by priority\n- **backoffQ**: Pods that failed and are backing off\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods that can't be scheduled now\n\n#### **Pod Movement Triggers**\n- Pod creation/update \u2192 added to activeQ\n- Pod rejected unschedulable \u2192 moved to backoffQ\n- Long unschedulable pod \u2192 expires from unschedulablePods to activeQ\n- Cluster event (node added, resource freed) \u2192 pods requeued via `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()`\n\n#### **Queueing Hints (plugin EnqueueExtensions)**\nPlugins can register `EventsToRegister()` to specify which cluster events should requeue pods they rejected:\n- Avoids unnecessary requeuing\n- Improves scheduling efficiency\n- Plugins return QueueingHint for events they care about\n\n### Error Handling & Recovery\n\n#### **Scheduling Cycle Failures**\n1. **PreFilter failure** \u2192 Mark all nodes unschedulable, trigger PostFilter\n2. **Filter/Score failure** \u2192 Continue with other nodes or fall through\n3. **PostFilter (preemption)** \u2192 Attempts to preempt pods to make room\n4. **Reserve failure** \u2192 Calls `Unreserve()` on all plugins, forgets pod\n\n#### **Binding Cycle Failures**\n1. **PreBind/Bind failure** \u2192 Trigger `Unreserve()`, forget pod from cache\n2. **Assumed pod expires** \u2192 Cache automatically forgets after TTL\n3. **Pod update during cycle** \u2192 Binding cycle detects and handles gracefully\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler v1.30.0 implements a sophisticated two-phase scheduling architecture that separates pod selection (scheduling cycle) from commitment (binding cycle). It uses an extensible plugin framework with 12 extension points, enabling both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to influence decisions without tight coupling. The scheduler maintains a priority-based queue and an intelligent cache that tracks node resources and assumed pod reservations. By using CycleState for isolation, snapshots for consistency, and the assume-release pattern for optimistic concurrency, the scheduler efficiently handles large clusters while allowing asynchronous binding without blocking other scheduling decisions. This design enables high throughput and low latency pod scheduling while maintaining correctness and extensibility.\n\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

  "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler is responsible for assigning unscheduled Pods to Nodes. It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** \u2014 Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** \u2014 Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)\n\n### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** \u2014 Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** \u2014 `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** \u2014 `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** \u2014 `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** \u2014 `cacheImpl` maintaining node information, tracking assumed pods, and managing cache assumptions\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** \u2014 Tree structure for efficient node lookup\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** \u2014 Immutable snapshot of cache taken at scheduling cycle start\n\n### Event Handling & Extenders\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** \u2014 Event handlers for pod/node/storage class updates triggering queue requeuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** \u2014 HTTP-based external scheduler extender interface\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. **Entry Point: Scheduler Initialization & Run**\n   - **`scheduler.New(ctx, client, informerFactory, ...)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:253)\n     - Creates in-tree plugin registry\n     - Builds scheduler profiles and framework instances\n     - Initializes scheduling queue (PriorityQueue)\n     - Initializes scheduler cache\n     - Registers event handlers for pods/nodes\n     - Returns `*Scheduler` instance\n\n   - **`sched.Run(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435)\n     - Starts scheduling queue goroutines\n     - Launches main scheduling loop via `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)`\n\n### 2. **Main Scheduling Loop**\n   - **`sched.ScheduleOne(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66)\n     - Calls `sched.NextPod(logger)` \u2192 pops from `SchedulingQueue`\n     - Retrieves framework for pod's scheduler name\n     - Calls **`sched.schedulingCycle(ctx, state, fwk, podInfo, start, podsToActivate)`** (line 111)\n     - On success, launches binding cycle in goroutine\n\n### 3. **Scheduling Cycle (Pod Selection)**\n   - **`schedulingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:139)\n     1. Calls **`sched.SchedulePod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`** \u2192 **`sched.schedulePod()`** (line 390)\n        - Updates cache snapshot via `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n        - **Phase A: Filtering**\n          - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`\n          - Runs **PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` (line 453)\n          - Calls **`findNodesThatPassFilters()`** (line 573)\n            - Runs **Filter plugins** in parallel via `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` (line 640)\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)` per node\n          - Processes extender filters via `findNodesThatPassExtenders()`\n        - **Phase B: Scoring**\n          - Calls **`prioritizeNodes()`** (line 425)\n          - Runs **PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n          - Runs **Score plugins** on each feasible node via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n          - Scores with extenders (if present)\n        - **Phase C: Selection**\n          - Calls `selectHost()` to pick best-scored node\n\n     2. On success, **assumes pod** via `sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, nodeName)` (line 198)\n        - Adds pod to cache with assumed state\n\n     3. Runs **Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` (line 209)\n        - If fails, calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n\n     4. Runs **Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` (line 231)\n        - Creates waiting pods if any plugin returns \"Wait\"\n\n### 4. **Binding Cycle (Pod Commitment)**\n   - **`bindingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:265)\n     1. Waits on **Permit plugins** via `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` (line 278)\n\n     2. Runs **PreBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` (line 294)\n        - Performs pre-binding validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n\n     3. Runs **Bind plugins** via `sched.bind()` (line 299)\n        - Default: calls API server to create Pod binding\n        - Can be overridden by custom bind plugins\n\n     4. Runs **PostBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` (line 312)\n        - Informational, performs cleanup/logging\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Plugin Framework Architecture**\nThe scheduler uses an **extension point** pattern where plugins implement specific interfaces and hook into well-defined points in the scheduling pipeline:\n\n```\nExtension Points (in execution order):\n\u251c\u2500 PreEnqueue (before pod enters activeQ)\n\u251c\u2500 QueueSort (sorts pods in queue)\n\u251c\u2500 PreFilter (pod-level filtering setup, can filter out nodes)\n\u251c\u2500 Filter (per-node filtering, parallel execution)\n\u251c\u2500 PostFilter (preemption/recovery if no nodes fit)\n\u251c\u2500 PreScore (informational, after filtering)\n\u251c\u2500 Score (per-node scoring, parallel execution)\n\u251c\u2500 Reserve (mark node as having resources reserved)\n\u251c\u2500 Permit (final gate before binding, can wait)\n\u251c\u2500 PreBind (validation before binding)\n\u251c\u2500 Bind (performs actual binding)\n\u2514\u2500 PostBind (post-binding cleanup)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n- the scheduler to continue scheduling other pods while binding happens asynchronously.\n\n#### 3. **State Isolation via CycleState**\nEach scheduling cycle creates a fresh `CycleState` that plugins use # Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis

## Overview

The Kubernetes scheduler is responsible for assigning unscheduled Pods to Nodes. It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.

---

## Files Examined

### Core Scheduler Files
- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points
- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)

### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution

### Scheduling Queue & Cache
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — `cacheImpl` maintaining node information, tracking assumed pods, and managing cache assumptions
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — Tree struct
... (truncated)
